O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	To you, my very dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its contents, and I have made an end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is strong in our region and entirely foreign everywhere else, the science has perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that hands have turned.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this have come the errors and the vanities, and closed are the attentions and alienated is the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revitalize together the arrangement of this treatise according to the method of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and will come together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of other tools of the work with the adjustment of the explanation and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who engages in this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galens says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of them, and the movement of the moving veins and the resting ones, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should beware lest he fall into error and injure people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus, I have seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon themselves to their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut the abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for so much blood gushed out that the woman fell dead at his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another doctor who was extracting a stone from a man's eye, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he carried away with it a piece of the membrane, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it was cut out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another doctor who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctors full of ignorance bind the fracture on the wound with splints by strong tie, and leave no padding to the wound at all, and leave it thus for a long time;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commands that he does not untie it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remains thus until the leg is entirely swollen and the feet and comes to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I untied it, it was in peace and he felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But nevertheless, the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not stop from spreading through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another doctor who bursts the infected abscess and then inflames it due to the maliciousness of his rule.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place where one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for that reason, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is, work where there is danger in various positions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For that reason, it is necessary that you be cautious so that foolish physicians cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your arms in discussion, and undertake your patients lightly yet firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you arrive at success and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the appalling diseases of severe illness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove the weapons from that which causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not undertake a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauterizations and medicinal cauterizations, and the chapters are arranged from head to toe;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the forms of ointments, and the instruments for cauterization, and everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the head to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	In order that we may remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of the aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest discourse and subtlest science and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many of the wise have spoken about this and agreed upon it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and they mock a little with their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery universally helps all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have differentiated and said that cautery is of great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not useful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for a hot disease, nor with dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and says he who said the opposite that cautery provides great help to hot and dry disease that comes into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the disposition of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any way, let no one interfere except those who have experienced it and who understand through long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of human temperaments, and the conditions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and the span of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have no fear of other temperaments, especially in cold and wet diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery together with fire is among the secrets of treatments, and of greater goodness than cauterization by burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it only affects the member that is burnt, and does not harm another member unless by chance.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines move from one member to another in the distant parts and cause severe diseases to come to the member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perchance kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is not an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this have I found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself for the length of speech, for it does not please me that I remove the secret which is stored in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauteries should be made, and chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harmful thing coming from below is removed by means of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cautery is for necessary pains that are severe and urgent which cannot wait until a time when greater mischief does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, for cautery is a medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause of pain, and it acts faster than other medicines because of its power and the virtue of its effect and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is a powerful thing that the disease may come sometimes according to the temperament of the patient and the site of the disease and its property;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as tooth cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is effective after medicine, but their understanding is false, and cauterization is the last of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they are ineffective, then we apply the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient said that cauterization with a golden instrument is better than with iron, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and the excellence of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the flame of cauterization does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and have found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauterization with gold is better than with iron, just as they said it to be.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And nevertheless, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	so they do at the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have prepared appropriately for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and it is used twice due to a disease called "soda," and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a dissolving medicine modifying the head for three or four nights, according to what the strength and age and habit of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then shave the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit between your hands crossed, and place his hands on some weight;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterward place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and there where your middle fingers will come, bleed from the joint then heat the cautery which is called "olivary", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	and place it on the marked spot with ink, and do so by loosening and tightening your hand little by little while turning it around;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and return to the spot if you see the bone slightly protruding;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after take some tar, and put it in water and mix cotton within, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after put on linen moistened in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave on until the scalding is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the wound with the ointment which is called "tetrafarmacon," until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, it aids movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some say that one should leave the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it should be cleaned.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that the cautery should be left on for a long time and pressed so hard that it abates the bone as wide as the thread that women put in their spindles so that the humors are forced out;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards it must be cleaned and soaked.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to be entirely good in every case, except in some people where there is reason for fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulder is weakened by the continuous dislocations of nature, as we testify in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and likewise when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is safer and better for me, and with this method I work towards a wholesome union.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When throughout the head comes chronic pain, and lasts for a long time, then the patient must use hyrises and pills which are called "cochie", and cleansing of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we have mentioned before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the shoulder of the patient is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize below that cautery a bit as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After make cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place which is called "vasselz";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and there are places where one applies leeches;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see until the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cautery for the horns be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in a part of the head comes sudden pain, and the disease extends to the eye, and the brain is cleansed with purgative medicines, and all other treatments that I have mentioned in the section on diseases are performed, yet none of this helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then make cauterization according to two methods, that is to say with moist medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with moist medicine is that you take a piece of fig, and remove the peel and cut it to one part in two parts for the shoulders, and then make an incision on the temple where the pain lies in such a manner that you can place the piece of fig under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, then bind it tightly and leave it like that for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie it and remove the piece of garlic, and leave the wound like that for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply cotton soaked in butter until the pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of anointing until he is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish to use some of the burning medicines that I have written about in the eleventh treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a ball where it has a bit of curvature, and in the middle has a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little gently, until half of the thickness of the kerb is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so the artery does not burn, which is on the outside, and let an abundance of blood flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After put cotton in the eye of seil, and put on the place for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put cotton moistened in butter, and then clean the place of ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare," at all the tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this recent migraine.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizations previously mentioned of medicine and iron do not suit him, then you must heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and sign before on the painful place a line of half an inch long, and take your hand away once, and hold back so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jaw that moves when one eats, and the nerve should not be looked at so that it moves and spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of the flow of blood from the artery when it will be cut, for cutting has great fear especially for those who are not knowledgeable, and who are not scholars and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work halfway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have described in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from cold comes into the ear, and one has applied solutive medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section, and the pain does not diminish, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncture all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a bit away from the root of the ear once you have marked the spot to incise;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture which should be treated by cauterization is none other than those that move phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not apply cauterization to those that come from dryness and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this kind of torture that moves phlegm with hydrous and evacuations from the head and gargling, and if this does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a bit outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery directly at the top of the ear below the horn of the head by a bit, and another one on the temple as long as a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on top until the middle of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it resembles the knife that we have described before, but it is a bit finer and the knife must be a bit thicker;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after care the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large drafts and pills that purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after raising the head of the patient completely, and place on the occiput the mustard plaster which is written in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	if he is healed thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then make three cauteries around the head descending to the neck, and have one inch of space between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you see to adjust, and the patient is enduring, make one cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two corners, and treat until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterization which is called "olivare" be as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of sores and what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterwards shave the head of the patient, then apply cauterization in the middle of the head and on each corner, and one at the back and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is enduring, and the disease is strong, apply four cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and he lets it until the most of the heat is burned, and lifts your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until it is healed, and let the cautery which is called "olivary" that we have mentioned before be used.
de l’epilempsie	of the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and one must first modify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffering from deep medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make him gargle and chew, frequently modifying the brain with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	afterwards, cut the head in half, and make the cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the basin, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and enduring, make cauteries as I have said for one who has paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olivary according to the method that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is inflamed, make a fine cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy the excesses or the moisture is corrupted and phlegm is thick, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities incline towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what is mentioned previously in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After raise the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after make the linen bandage well done, just like the circle, and put it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient sits crossed, and be well held on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after present the ointment, and it is worth using wool of old barberry;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it with moderate fire, so that when the hand touches it, it can be tolerated;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after empty the circle inside around the head, and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient once each week with another good treatment, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	For if you wish to cauterize it, make several points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This kind of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on wet cotton in butter and in goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye ointment
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the ailment first comes to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient drink that purifies the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After that, instruct him to lean his head back, and perform a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on both temples if the tearing of the eye is in both eyes together, or one if it is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart with the entire cautery, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of blood flow, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with whatever power you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how you will probe it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And sometimes a cautery or hot iron is used under the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	from the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are on the outer appearance of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic excesses, then he makes the cautery that I have said at the beginning of this chapter below the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	One cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries with hot iron under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is need for more, then cautiously cauterize above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient to drink three nights of cochos.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olive cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations with the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called «olivary».
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you want to make two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand there except until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes turn inward and prick the eye, and a cautery is performed according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, with fire, or with burning medication.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then place the patient in your care;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after place on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as if of the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton in egg white and marjoram powder on the eye, then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	after cautery on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, so that the hair is burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retract, and the hairs rise at the edge of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moist cotton in butter until the burn is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of anointing until he is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	and if afterward the hairs grow back and the scab softens, then restart the cautery on that same spot as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are weaker, then cauterize until the scab is lifted to its natural place, and they are even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fire cauterization is when you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even, then make a shape of mirtle leaf from parchment;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and quicklime, of each three parts, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread over the shape as you are made like the leaf of myrtle, and place on the paper of the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease is only in one eye, then work on that one, and if in both equally;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye moistened cotton in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the head of the patient should be in your hand and place your finger showing on the medicine, and press the pouch and the swelling every time the patient feels the sting of the medicine, for it stings as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine properly.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the stinging has passed, then remove the cloth, and check if you see the paper raised as if it were lifted by the constraint of fire or by an incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	and if it is not so, then apply more of the medicine on the spot where the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are set properly;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply moistened cotton in butter until the burnt pus falls out, then treat the area of the ointment which is called "diaphoretic" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you be careful with your work with great care that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	and if the parchment becomes soft afterward, and the hairs prick in the eye, then reapply the medicine on that area which has been softened by the parchment properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the care until he is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be denied to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head on your thigh;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move, nor does he remove his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after put moist cotton in egg white or in juice of solanum on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heat the cautery which is blue:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is attached to the head like the form of an arrow feather, along with which should be the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you want, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it can also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nonetheless, this one that is attached is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	after press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then open it, and draw out the bowel forcefully;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after put on the cautery very hot, and hold your hand at the cautery at the part of the nose below the eye, so that your hand does not make foolishness;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery until the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and again if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after put on moist cotton in butter, and cure it with the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and heal it according to what would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand about fistula, and open the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after put in the cut some subtle camphor of this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and add to the quantity of a .3. of plum;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand on the camphor firmly, and the patient must not move at all, until the melted plum does not run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye cotton moistened in egg white or in oil;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the plum thus dries the area of the fistula and heals it with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a purge to the patient, and to bring the fistula back to its proper place in the body according to what is appropriate.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks appear on the lips which are called "hairs", and especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks that we have mentioned in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat the small scalpel cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it hastily into those fissures until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after care the area with cerote until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the tongue or in the throat, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes putrefied and rotten and is stagnant and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not help:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must have the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	then apply it to the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and in the back area;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do it thus once or twice after the treatment of what we have said in treatments until he is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that does not work, then place the head of the patient on your knee;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heat the cautery in such a way that you place a cane on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put inside the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift your hand and restart the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after the patient fills his mouth with salty water, and keeps it for an hour and spits out afterwards.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth which was moving is confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from cold, or there is cold in the gum, and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to use cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery of butter and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the end in a iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after take cotton and wrap on the tip of a tent, and anoint with boiled butter, and put on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you want, anoint wool and cotton with cold butter, and put on the painful tooth, and place hot iron over it until the fire reaches the edge of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauterization is such that you take a cane of iron or bronze, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	after heat the cauterizing tool, of which the form will be mentioned later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizing tool is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cautery, and then forcefully spit it out;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery on the head as you desire, and according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	Of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not responsive to digestion through medicines, then heat the cautery as described hereafter comes the form, and have two openings for the smoke to exit from the other side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like this for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and place moist cotton in butter on it until the burn is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after care the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the reed:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moisture overcomes the nasal channels, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with dissolving medications;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after you make cautery at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not go as far as the throat itself, nor burn from the heart but a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	after you make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cautery which is called "clavile" be as we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the lint
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	when all the diseases of consumption are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the disease is long-standing, then make two cauteries on the shoulder in their place;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and the other cautery between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery which is called "clavile" be according to the form that was previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking with the entire cautery which is called "poin" of which the form is mentioned earlier in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be up to thirty, or around there.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the place according to what was previously said, let the cauterization be three inches according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for that reason, the cauterizations are lighter, because you do three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first treat the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After, place the patient on their back and on their side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after, lift the kernel that is inside the titillite with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two horns thus is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the boil until it penetrates to the bone, and the shape of the cautery comes together with four cauters;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery which has three prongs, so the shapes of the cauteries are six cauters;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent and that is the form of the cautery which has three prongs:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve so there are eight cauters.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery pared pigs with fat;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After make rest the patient, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then make a cautery on the thick part of the collarbone, or many cauterizations by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold and much moisture that it alters its temperament, and are multiplied the catarrhs to him, and in the customary ways of treatment it does not profit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From this point on, make three cauterizations: one below the nipple of the breast for the quantity of a bean, to the entire cautery clavicle, and two cauterizations outside the two sides such that the figure of the cauterizations be at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they cast pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterizations be so deep that they reach the two parts of the lung, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cautery, cautery by pricking and bleeding on the stomach one spot according to the quantity that you wish to remove;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the care that we have had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes to have pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, so much that it is greatly displaced from its natural temperament by the excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then the patient must be bled from his hepatic vein;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and bleed from three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the person come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and there be space between each cautery the thickness of a thumb;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long on the body, and do not press too much with your hand over the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let only half of the heart be burned, and let the patient stand on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the cutellaire, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the entire heart, for you would cause the whole body to wither;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not reach up to the boil, for the skin is very delicate in that area, and you know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When it has abscessed in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, then the patient feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment is necessary, the patient must be shaved on their head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then apply a poultice to the area where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles the ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the blood is burned, and comes down to the siphon, until all putrefaction is completely expelled;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of the wounds until he is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not fitting that anyone should use this cautery except those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have sometimes failed.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly work, and yet it seems to me that sometimes it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery ofpleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make plasters from the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristolochia, the longest that you can find, and it should be dry, and as thick and as long as your thumb;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and the mortar in oil, and press it to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the jaw and the neck, and two small cauters a bit downward in the part which is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauters between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly to the back;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the sides of the breast outside the cautery which is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but do it openly as in an unguent.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancient ones say that some men use a fire cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess;
