et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and on which are swollen and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids are heated, and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "treatment for contusion," and it is that you make behind the patient who has this disease the hairs which he has on his forehead, then make III cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the cuts be like two fingers right in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose, and the other two at the sides above the eyelids, and beware of the arteries that are on both sides above the eyelids;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and move your hand away from the joining of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to wipe the blood, then put the sharp spatula in two parts where this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is below the temple up to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and peel all the heart that is between the two cuts to the whole surface which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so place in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side towards the diseased flesh of the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous up to where it opens from the heart, and then make another one in the middle cut up to the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw the blood evenly, and press the area for the captured blood;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then place in each incision a wad of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened with wine and oil and ash, and be careful that hot abscesses do not come;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply a great deal of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used to heal wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the realm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When acute catarrh often comes to someone, and you see the eyes dull and small, and weakening of sight, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and on the head it causes acute pain, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know by these symptoms that those materials and the catarrh come from many veins, and the best treatment there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie down on his back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one on the wide temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And start from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go as far as the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the wound and put old cotton and linen threads in it;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind above with cloths moistened in wine and in oil, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you must rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances, which promote the hardening of the cartilage.
En teil maniere:	In such manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to these wounds to promote the hardening of cartilage throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	for grains, for beasts, for stone from mines or similar things such as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	for seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	for flowing things such as water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill a bit of violet oil or flaxseed oil, then apply extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make the person sneeze with condiments, and plug the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and pull the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Very often force comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if force does not come, the administrator should perform extraction with subtle tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If force comes with the tweezers, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then perform the extraction with a subtle needle of small double edge;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out by this means, then make a tube of lead and insert the end of the tube into the opening of the ear tightly, and plug what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then draw the force strongly, for often comes the force as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out by force in such manner, then take glue of egg and use some instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw out by force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	and if it does not come out by force from all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear before a hot abscess and spasm comes.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the method of the incision is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and withdraw blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat where it hangs.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be like a moon, until you come to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer the spatula gently according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and to administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with fine tweezers and the suction tube, as we have said, so that the extraction may be light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of fluid that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing with condiments first, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the fluid is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger thin and light, and warm them a bit in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and have the patient place one in the opening of his ear, and jump up with one of his feet from the other side, and strike with another stone upon the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop doing this from stone to stone until the pain goes away completely, and thus it will all go away;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you want to, take some reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end into fire until the softer part of the reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another section with other incisions until all the pus comes out, just as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small body, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the section on division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large body that can be felt, then apply the extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the lightest thing to remove that may be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of earwigs from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look into the ear toward the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any hairs there, pull them out with subtle tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the tube that has this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully on the entire tube;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff around the tube with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the excision of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and then distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	and whether it is of silver or brass, narrow below at the small openings, and above wider for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside for the distillation, an instrument of brass well made for this purpose, and if you want, take the rasp and wrap around the point appropriately with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines into the cane, and the cane should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then insert the rasp into the cotton completely, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled into the ear canal;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be slightly heated over fire before you distill it into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	Some children are born who have no openings in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to adults due to obstructions from wounds or foreign objects inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes occur deep within the ear so that they cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the opening is slightly blocked, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Then the one that comes in perfect, if it cannot be seen, is of grievous healing in many conditions, and in that which can be seen you must place the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the obstruction apparent, then the work has all this space wherein is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting on both sides entirely smooth, so that it does not hurt the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the obstruction is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and cut lightly until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is fully in the ear, then take a fine light scraper and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the core of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the wax that causes the patient to have difficulty hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is sealed, or you take a plug and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the plug and insert another moistened with an ointment made of rose oil and wax until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papermakers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This eyelid that comes over the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch it with forceps and tweezers, and cut it from its roots with a spatula;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put ground vitriol on the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not heal, then cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is very good;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and they often recur if any part of their roots remains;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come into the eyes things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail", and it is a gathering of moisture thickened above and below the eye.
li ovraiges est telz:	the work is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	be wary if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	then make an incision widely, then gently peel each part, then take it with tweezers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing a little the eye membrane, it does no harm to the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, then it is sewn with a stitch, and treated until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, then do not apply force, for the ointments restore it quickly and promote flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the earwax is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the paper, and extend the earwax with tweezers, and cut and press it from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, it does not matter;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the earwax is cut, then apply salt water, and treat the area with flesh-growing medicine until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is wrapped in the webbing of the eyelids above, and this happens more to children than to any people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep there, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are wet which swells and the appearance is covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your hands and feel the protrusion between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the method of the work is that the patient places his head on your healthy [part];
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then place it on top;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your hands from one side to the other so that the protrusion is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut into the moisture with a sharp spatula a wide slit, and let it not be larger than the wound one makes at the edge of a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut through the skin thoroughly until you reach the protrusion;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in various positions, the protrusion comes out of the slit, according to the form of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it with a piece of coarse cloth held between your hands, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and guard that you do not apply to the fissure, that you do not come all the way to the spleen until the eye, that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	and if the abscess does not open at the beginning of the fissure, enlarge the fissure slightly until it opens;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind coal and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When on the eyelids hairs grow in a manner different from natural, and they are irritated, they harm the eyes, and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and leukoma, to the point that it can lead to the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the treatment is according to four manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery with fire, or by medicinal baths according to what is mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by splints, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle with the entire thread on top;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be near the margin of the paper where the hair grows next to these hairs, and draw the thread across the entire paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut into the part below the parchment, below the attached hairs, cutting all the spatumile, from the large eyelid to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread, and place below the parchment a small tent of cotton and cloth, then apply on the parchment a figure of henna, like the leaf of myrtle, and it always befits that the figure should according to the quantity you wish to lift the divided parchment.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And there are cases where it is necessary to cut a large quantity of the parchment according to how softened the parchment is;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then cut through the entire spatumile along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large eyelid to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs with a thickness of a root, then insert the lancet into one of the two corners of the circle, then peel it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then bring the two lips together with a stitch of one needle using fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and apply heat to remove the excess threads on both eyebrows using some sticky substances, if you wish to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then do not bother, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without stitching with drying and binding substances, for the bandage rises with the closing of the wound and its joining, but the stitch is weaker (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and there is another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, at three inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you are not able to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with a thread, and insert it through the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and place one thread next to the large eyelid, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads evenly between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with poultice and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are inverted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the suturing in one and the other is more intricate.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of the veins is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you invert the paper and cut into it according to what I have said, and then make two veins by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and as wide as the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at the two shoulders of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then carefully join one and the other above what surpasses of the paper of the eye, and extract the two canals from the two parts completely;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it this way for some days, and the skin that was constricted will die, dry out, and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, cut it with force, then clean it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sealed, and the paper is lifted, the hairs will no longer prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a thread of silk smooth and fine;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then gather the shoulders and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the case another fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then have the patient place their head on your knee;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is delicate and fine work, then insert the needle entirely into the case at the root of the hair adjacent, and pierce it quickly into the parchment until you pull it over the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the socket, and place that hair into the socket if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then withdraw your hand until the hair comes out entirely from the socket into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the socket is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the socket downward along the entire thread that you have arranged, until the socket comes out of the hole above and you can see it with your eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then pull the socket and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair burns in its place and new flesh grows over;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hair is short, then accompany the long hair from the natural hair, and lift it with that which you leave, until it is extended and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pus from the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes to the eye, it happens in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by the suddenness of a wound, or of a cutting or of a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the method of treatment is that you cut open that swelling, separate its lips, and put linen threads inside, and leave it until it heals;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not appropriate that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, then the illness returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but use softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the ash of water or earth and flaxseed should be cooked, and unguents of aquilon melted in any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a cloth, and it is cured with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not heal in the same form as before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and cut and cautery and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyelid to the right, so that the thread comes out two fingers from the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it to one spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is appropriate, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take a scraper and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on the sides inside the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the points of the two fissures of the two corners of the incision that you have made be such that when they are brought together, the shape should resemble the form of a letter called “I Greek”;
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its edges are sharp below, from what lies under the skin, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a fissure or a suture or a cautery, then you must make a clean incision below the hairs of the skin, according to what is stated above;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two leaves of a tent, just as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters devise ingeniously to the best of their ability how they might restore the figure to its natural state;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is required of work and instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this soldering happens to men in such a way that the eyelid above is fused with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the eyelid, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and you stretch with pincers until you cut what is near the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear a too sharp spatula to hurt the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision, with which you peel that assembly, be slight, so that the parchment returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it heals all that assembly, and they sometimes use salty water in the sharp eye, and raise with sweet water, and of collar.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then place between the parchment and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool moistened in egg white;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day use the collar and the sudatory things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail grows in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another that is not nervous, but resembles white frozen moisture, which when one touches it with iron and tries to pare it with tweezers, one cannot.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both appearances begin near the large eyelid, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the method of the incision is that the patient place his head in your hand, then operate on the eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper to your hand, then curl the nail with small double-edged tweezers, and stretch it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put horse hair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the tip of the needle a bit and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way through the nail, and tie the nail with thread and stretch it above, and shave all the hair next to the nail which is near the pupil and attach the silk to the hair until the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct very finely and gently, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision the usual flow of tears does not come from the eye;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail extends only to the ounce, and to the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one peels off all the sputamile [likely a misspelling or archaic term, possibly meant to be "peritame" or similar], from which this form comes;
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	and be careful that the sputamile does not touch the flesh membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, put a bit of ground seal and some collyrium made of litharge in the eye, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not firm, and you cannot push the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail is often treated with medicine;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, work on the patient's eye, and take the lightly sharpened spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the nail above subtly, and if you see that it does not thin out and the quick is pressing in, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyria made of litharge and of red collyrium and well ground, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then restart the work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If any thing does not oppose you in the eye, like a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye with great damage, suspend it to the lancet, and cut part of it and not all, so tears may come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill red collyrium into the eye which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and spreading over the membranes and turning them outward, and it resembles a rose of balausteon;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the procedure is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you operate on the eyes, and cut all that flesh with suitable tweezers for this, and hold it firmly;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first part, and keep cutting close to the skin until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the work;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and the incision of the spatula that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and for small forces from which one removes the splinter, just as the form after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of selenium ground to which you add red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top cotton with egg white so that it secures a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if anything remains and the skin swells above it, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when shards are set in the eye by this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	but nonetheless you must lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and by the accidental way in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is able to endure that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Sebel are red veins that cover the eye, and they hinder sight's work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is then necessary first that you look if the eye in which the cataract is, is strong, and there is no other disease besides the cataract;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then suspend those veins for all the ancyons according to your wisdom, and let the ancyons be twice as fine according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then you coil with force those fine veins, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move out of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at noon in the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut outside those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red collyria to corrupt what remains of the bile.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have the power to gather all of this in that hour, make a plaster on the eye with things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and assured of a hot abscess, then restart according to this method which is before until he be healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The doctor calls a fistula "arissati":
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you cure it with cautery and with fiery medicine according to what I have said before, and if it is not healed, then there is reason in it that you cut into the abscess, where it must die, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then clean it all with this instrument of which here is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "harsh head," and it should be made of iron to the head round, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the area of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the area is sealed, and flesh grows, and the core of the bone is sealed, and remains this way for forty days, and it does not renew or become abscessed, and no harmful accidents occur, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, then there is another method to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron and with medicinal waters, and when it is uncovered then take the forceps according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and let the handle be tapered up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the forceps entirely until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it because air comes out if they hold their hand over their nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medications, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the wound hardens, the matter will go to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye is completely open in its entirety, and there comes no obstruction to the nose, nor any diminishment, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heal it, then apply cupping or leeches without piercing to draw out, then place on the eye a mixture of acacia and aloe and frankincense and storax, and then extract the eye, and plaster over it with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the method of the cloths is that you take cloths sufficiently soft, and double each one four times, and then place one over the other according to the amount the eye requires;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain over a hard bandage firmly, and begin the cupping to suction without pricking;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping and keep the eye strained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, you must strain them greatly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye returning to its place, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then restart the plaster and the bandages and the binding and the cupping until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the breaking of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come to the uvea tissue, then it opens, and small pieces like grains of resin appear, and it is astounding to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you want to cut it off, the work is such that you insert a needle at the root of the part below up to the one above, then insert another needle where there is the doubled thread from the part of the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut at the place of the doubled thread and tie a part of the grape around, and tighten well, then remove the needle and apply moistened wool soaked in egg white to the eye;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread falls off with the grape, then clean the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And sometimes the wound is restrained by a hoop of cloth around it on all sides until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows great opacity, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in through the pupil, and draw out the white moisture and lower the eye, and insert it thus immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than a bow that is gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of its appearance is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take his head in both your hands, and move it until you see the bow come up to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it is fixed, and does not descend and the light is dispersed, and the patient sees things as they were before;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the pus is not regulated as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then seat the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut on the corneal membrane a spot by continuing along the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona until the pus comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, then drip into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then clean it with other treatments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	so we work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the sun's light, and bind the healthy eye tightly and hold it very firmly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almond," or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the tip of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a nail in that membrane of the eye at the part of the lower eyelid, then insert the instrument which is called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces through the membrane of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the length of the path of almagda be exactly to the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black part;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	you will see the bone through that membrane because of the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the aqueous is, then press it under one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the aqueous humor is now deficient, the patient sees something before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest a little, and if the liquid rises through the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and it does not rise, then extract alum lightly by turning your hand bit by bit;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put in water a bit of seal jewel, and wash the eye with that.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye tufts or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin mixed with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And pierce then only the conjunctive, and do not go too deep, but make the place delicate, then put alum in it, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable place to sleep, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be devoid of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be tied according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not fitting that you do this at the time of the treatment or after the incision immediately, but it is necessary that you lighten this, because the humor rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if warm abscesses come, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and address it with what alleviates abscesses;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calmed, unbind the gaze and place on his face a patch to cover for some days, and let him be immediately in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	and then leave the house little by little, and get accustomed to his case;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from Yemen, who told us that in his country they make a device pierced, to which one draws out water, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, for those who do not understand them see;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be properly made of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of the axes of this same fineness, and the back in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes diverse kinds of charred attachments are born, from which some resemble scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and there are such where the char is embedded in a fox color, and it has smooth skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case, with the smooth char and not embedded, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and work his nostrils, and apply the ointment to those charred areas, and pull them hard;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then cut what you can support with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	and if there remains anything that cannot be cut, then open it completely with fine light instruments gently, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it swells up on you, or an abscess becomes hot, then treat it as appropriate;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the swelling is subdued and all the flesh is removed, then apply crushed henbane and vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the henbane works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is flesh grown in the bone above, to which the instruments do not reach to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put in a thread of linen somewhat thick, and be knotted by our hands, and have between each knot a space one inch or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and have the patient place the head of the thread in their nose with some force, and draw it through until it comes from inside the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often do children in schools do this, and it is an easy thing for those who wish to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the end that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart little by little along the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the gnats have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the nose a bandage of linen for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the head, to which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit is similarly;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have the handle at the head to hold it when you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Often, a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large quickly, to the point that it is noticeable when looking at it;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason, you should cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then apply the cautery or burning medicine to the area;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a dusky color, or lacks sensation:
