si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	Do not touch it with iron for it is an infected abscess, for when one cuts into it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of a white appearance, not of a bloody color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then empty the patient and cut it out without fear, and treat the area with drying and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilaginous works, it benefits little, for in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, one should examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two edges with a suture, then treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, then you must peel all the parts of their surface until they heal, then join the two edges with a suture, and bind it tightly, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense over it;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put the powders on a piece of plaster of Paris or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of the suture is that you bring together the edges:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Some men have within their lips abscesses that are hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn the lips inside out, and cut into each knot, and take them with forceps and cut in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the place after the incision of ground vitriol, until the blood is stilled;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash with oil, and clean the area of dry matters until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply ground vitriol to the area, or other binding and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	so it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the impurities
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, bark-like things that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and decayed, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	so it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulders be in your lap, and remove the teeth or the bark-like things that appear, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other spots, until they are cleansed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is there at the first reason, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then start again the second day and the third, until you have it all clean;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers used to clean between the teeth have different shapes than those used to clean the surfaces of the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay drawing it as long as you can, for no one should do so at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for this is a very high quality substance so that one has no excuse for failing.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract, you must be certain of the painful tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain is on the patient, and they think it is in the tooth, and they pull out the good tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and nevertheless the pain does not leave because of this, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already wanted to do this to these saints;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the painful tooth, then you must peel around the tooth for about one finger's breadth strongly to protect the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your hands or with fine tweezers little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the tweezers;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the shoulder of the patient be in your hands between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push inside on each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	and if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with cloths where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and then grasp it carefully with tongs so that it does not break when grasping;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well wary that you do not break it and leave a part behind, which may return to the patient through the mischief of the root causing greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	and beware that you do not act as the ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the socket, and do not administer what we have mentioned;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause great illness through the extraction of those because of the roots that remain, or for the channels they break, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine or oil and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then apply the area with ground vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, with which one pulls teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be toothed to hold the teeth firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains outside, it is necessary that you put on the spot cotton moistened in butter for one or two days until the area is softened, then use the forceps which are called "algefri", from which the head seems like the beak of a goose;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and let them be made inside like a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out entirely with tongs, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and put in the instrument which is called “althali”, that is to say a lever, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by this means, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if this does not work, then use all the instruments, whose forms come after here:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which the form is here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are mentioned earlier in the discussion of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which the form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be strong so it cannot break, and know that many dental instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also of other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise subtle masters find their own instruments according to what their works and the diseases show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients taught no instrument due to the diversity; and if one breaks a cartilage or other bones where it could, then search for the suitable instruments that I have told you about, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well grasped to hold the bone so it does not slip but can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then scrape it all with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, especially in unmarried women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth, and it is not in the right place, and cannot be smoothed or filed:
adonques lou raie;	then pull it out;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is loose with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is shown here, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be of iron and sharp at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cutting little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file like the one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the steel with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then flatten it at the end for any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then it is necessary to file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth loosen, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot bite on what they eat without them falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, and that does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then they must be restrained with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then insert the threads between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach wisely up to the other healthy tooth;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin the wrapping until the part where you started, and withdraw your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the head of the thread with some forceps, and join them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not injure the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it so tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	it will remain and serve in this way for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two defective ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, it is reset in its place, fresh to fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is held tight as we have said, and remains and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this ligament comes under the tongue naturally, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a sutured wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you operate on the patient's mouth, and have his head in your hand, and lift his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nervous ligament widely so that the tongue is separated from its natural position, and if there is hardness or knotting, which is from a wound's suturing, then use a hooked instrument and cut widely at that ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and take care that the cut is not too deep, for the artery which is beneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift the area with rose water and salt, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen cloth;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the patient should comb each night so that the area does not become sealed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, then apply ground vitriol to the area;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the skin resists, then cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it of a pus color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining to the throat, and there is moisture, then apply a poultice, and cut it with a fine spatula, and deliver it from one side to the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the sweat hinders your work, then apply ground vitriol until it is dried out, then return to your work until you draw all the force out;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then raise the place from ash and soil, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes come into the throat lumps which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if they are hard abscesses of little sensation and of flesh color, then do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if they are red and the root is large, then do not touch them with iron, also to prevent blood flow;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave them until they are ripe, and then you shall divide them, or they will break on their own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if they are of white color and the root is delicate, then have the instrument ready to cut, but first check if the warm abscess has settled and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his shoulders be in your hands, and work on his mouth and take hold of the sergeant between your hands, and press the tongue below with all the instrument, which is its form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of silver or fine brass like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and put it in the center, and pull it out above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull something from the cloth with it, then cut it with the instrument, which is its form, that resembles forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and the head is curved all the same, and one part to another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	and it is sharp on one side, and dull on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water mixed with salt, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves have been boiled, or similar things, until the blood is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then just as you would the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman who had an abscess grow inside her throat, that is to say one small-sensed abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had nearly closed her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had put forth two streams through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then hurried and inserted a lancet into one [side], then pulled it out, and drew out a large portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then repair another part in the other nostril hole, and work the mouth and press the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after I inserted the lancet into these abscesses, and cut off a part, and no more than a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the conduit of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting into this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess grew again, filling the place that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I diagnosed it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus remains without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from those places, and do not know what God made of him after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the vein descends to the grape, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below, thick and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the red abscesses are calmed, and they are subtle, then you must cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and compact and is not elongated;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is blood-red or yellowish color or black, then you must avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is then necessary, when you see it according to the manner I have said, of its blueness and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we mentioned before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the needle into the grape, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut away more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more of it, you harm the voice, and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use ingenuity in the cautery of his fearful sense.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then you press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and clean with hot aqua fortis so that it is not too thick nor too thin;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the movement of this instrument, of which here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it should have on the head a spoon-like part where one puts the medicine, like the scoop of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat, and he is wounded;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a duration of half an hour, until you see it swollen and the irritation from the medicine be calmed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument wrapped in the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton burns on the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the fire of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around of the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be soaked in cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is more beneficial than the incision, or the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and horehound and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and put oil in it, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot have the instrument arranged according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	and whether it is of silver or bronze, and one of the pipes should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the tube until the eye is mortified;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after that, repeat it often until the eye dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the warm onset of an abscess, for many things can happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this except when the warm abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	and if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put inside the head an eggshell so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the eggshell does not cause the breath to trouble the mouth, and this is a good treatment together healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times, a bone or spine of fish, or some thing, sticks in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you must pull out what you can see, and press his tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move; 
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and that which is not apparent and is hidden in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	and perhaps the burned substance will be expelled by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navelwort, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie a string to the sponge, and then have it swallowed;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it reaches the place, it will catch fire, and then you will pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take the suction instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they may more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised up;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, lest it all come out, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient put in the instrument, so that they may move where the matter is pierced;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	so put it down and pull evenly with the entire instrument until it is firm.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the blood is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help at all, then look into the patient’s throat in the sunlight, since you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, then draw it out entirely with a small hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a horsehair cord, and insert it into the patient's throat, then heat the end of the horsehair cord, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, and work it in the mouth, and throw it inside to swallow, and move it often with his hand;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood tastes the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned for the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and let the pot be covered with a perforated lid in the middle, and through that hole be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you throw your fumigation in, and the patient puts the head of the cane in their mouth, and closes the mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes down to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will now fall, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation several times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient feel thirsty, and eat salty and sour things, and not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	and the form of the instrument with which one draws the blood, when it can be seen, resembles curved tweezers to easily enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a bird, and has the roughness of a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot leave;
et vez ci la forme:	and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the descriptions come afterward one by one in this book, and they differ in puncture and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways of which one is in its own likeness, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fleshly part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	and there are abscesses that one should not puncture until the pus is fully mature according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are those that need to be punctured when they are hard, and do not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it swells around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the puncturing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	when it is near the fundament, then it should be punctured before it becomes mature;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not right that you pierce an abscess hard without completed digestion, except for the one near the anus, which could not be perfected, and would extend inside, and a fistula comes.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the time of piercing the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is calmed, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the swelling and sharpening of the top of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must make the piercing at the lowest part of the abscess, and where it appears soft.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the puncture of the long body be, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before that, the body of its venom will be prolonged, and it is full of much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perchance harden the lips and the depths of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must treat small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many slits according to the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the heart, and cut;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become yellow like a flag, and is softened, then it should be treated as one treats buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the armpits;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and there are such where one makes a round incision, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a superficial abscess, you must pierce them completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then plug the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this multiple times gradually, until all the pus is released;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak vitality, or pregnant women, or small children, or old infirm men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the sneezing sometimes occurs with the discharge of pus, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, wipe the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a smooth wound, then apply pieces of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must place a tent in each one so that they come against each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have spread it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or linen cloth shavings without moisture, and bind it until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold and light water and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	and if the discharge of blood persists, then apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter time, and the area or the abscess is very nervous, then you must put on tents and cloths moistened in warm wine and oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the wound is fleshy, then you must put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess and wipe it and treat it as appropriate until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	for I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the pouches
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, they are like fibers that are in webs, just like the down of a chicken, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such as have moisture like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and some are so hard and stony to cut that there is no doubt if the artery does not hinder.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you test with all the instrument which is called "intromissory," from which the forms come after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open on top of the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is emptied, then peel without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when something is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and ash, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and this will remove what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	and then repeat with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know that nothing of the night remains;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with anointing as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds hard fat, then cut it according to this form, from the length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and sprinkle your medicines on it, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the matter where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery acts contrary, then do what I have told you after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the stony and moist abscess, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And there are some of these abscesses on the head that have no moisture, and among these was an abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess like a dull stone, rough and white, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck any of them, it would have made as much of a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming to the head, for those that come to the top of the children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that the pus may flow out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often this abscess occurs on the neck, and under the jawbones, and in the glands, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and they cluster together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	and each scrophula is properly within its coat, like the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the likenesses of these scrophules are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are such ones that contain moisture, and there are harmful ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves on both sides and is not adhered to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the windpipe, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	then you should cut it from above, and peel it on each side, and spread the two lips of the wound with forceps, if you need to, just as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and draw it out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let not the spatula be sharp or cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not go too deep, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this does not stop you from working, put in the wound ground vitriol or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to pus.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stanched, return to your work until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then examine closely if any small scrofula remains, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang down without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut away the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	and you must pay attention to cut the root of it, and pull hard, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula that hold superfluity, pierce them where it appears to mature;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it in the same way as the one mentioned before, while hanging, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then treat it with ointment that promotes flesh growth until it is healed.
de squinance	of sprain
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancient ones spoke and talked about the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a tracheal weakness, it is necessary that the fold of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be removed;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and no help is provided by this, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are affected by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the phlegm, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should make a small cut across below three rings or four, between the two rings or by the quantity of the surface cut, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and it is necessary for the section of the epiglottis that there be no flesh there, and the vessels are long to reach.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then he must stretch the skin of the throat to the full inch, then split the heart until it comes to the membrane;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the division of the phlegm from the membrane that jumps out through the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which one suspects strangulation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and sew it entirely except for the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is entirely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the defect becomes apparent.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to suture the wound and cleanse it, until it was cleansed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took a knife and stuck it in her throat and cut part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I knew that she had not cut a vein or artery but only the throat, and air was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the maiden except that she lost her voice, and later recovered her health;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for which I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess of a bluish-black color, and it often occurs in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natures, and accidents;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	for natural things have no design.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty substances, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not befit to work with fire except on that which is small, and it proves and searches throughout the introduction:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like fatty tissue and it cannot enter any vein, then cut it as one cuts the tissues, and remove it all together, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly all around, and treat it as appropriate, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods we have, of which I will speak all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that exists between knot and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that discharge is heat and fever lasting until the boiling stage has passed, and putrefaction is completed;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the knot, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a surface, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, oily, or moist, and very colorful as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the wound, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "introducer", according to what its form will come in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of investigating abscesses in the nose is that you take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the center, according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the probe, and be careful in this that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If running moisture comes out, whatever color it has, cut it open as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the probe no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly peel it from each side and watch the spot where it lies so you draw it out clean with the nose;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little of it remains and the skin troubles you, then apply to the wound some corrosive powders, bind up the wound, and put on things that soothe a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the pain is great, sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pulsating vein opposes you or something else makes you hurry, then use ground vitriol, and leave it there for two days or three, until the wound becomes putrid, and stop the boiling of the blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cut what remains of the knot.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the introductory instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are of three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used to stitch sores, and they are made of amber citrin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and those proven with black pitch are better for encircling the swellings of fistulas;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the pores.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of tumors are very diverse, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are tumors that have two curves in three ways as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are tumors that have three curves, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are tumors that have two curves, and tumors with only one curve, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these that we cut are sharp, and there are some that do not cut strongly except from one side, for which we scrape the skin, so that we do not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introducers, the needles are placed in tubes so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they are not used except in fleshy areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling onion skins, according to this form, with which blood is drained:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the site that heals with cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they resemble a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must sew according to this form from this line 2 up to 8:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then remove the fat, and apply a medicated salve to the wound, then sew the two edges of the wound together, and care for it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags downward and is softened due to its size, as often happens with women, then cut it open in two places on top, with two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of which one is held to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line 2 up to the line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then peel the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then clean it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula with edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.
