Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one heals someone with tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of black nightshade, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, it is lifted with oil of asphodel, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive accumulations should rise from old wine, or from juice water, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not right to bleed with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he should not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that he warms himself when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is bleeding is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with garlic, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and he should eat pulse, and castrated animal meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold temperament, let him take syrup of honey, and wine that is aromatic, moderate, which is between old and new, and let him eat roast porridge, and let him eat partridges and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will be cupped, he must drink more than he eats;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men at times treacle or mastic before cupping, or after, to strengthen the principal limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the soup be made delicate, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cups that are placed without pricking are those that are set upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and gout, and upon the belly and the throat and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not withstand pricking upon them, and it is only done to draw blood from member to member, as we place upon the breasts when the infant suckles;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity which is in the member, just as we put leeches on the belly and on the thigh to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and removes the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it may remove the obstruction or displace the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and it does so when applied to the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind, and these leeches are administered empty solely for suction;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the leech with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle one small hole, as if to pierce a needle, and let it be of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the middle have a crossbar of brass or iron to hold a lamp tightly, and let there be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the cups for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin different from those for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this cup in this way on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax candle or the liniment, and place it inside the cupping vessel across the wick that is inside the cupping vessel, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping vessel so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the openings that we have mentioned, so that when you want to, the steam comes out, and you remove the cupping vessel;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping vessel used for treating diseases of phlegm, entirely filled with water, there is no wick or openings, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed solely on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sinuses are not treated with bloodletting except in members where one cannot apply cupping due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in those parts bare of flesh, such as the toes or nails, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using them is that when you find sinuses that are in clear sweet waters without putrefaction, then you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place one at a time in sweet water, until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their insides;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let them be bled from veins and with cupping, then rub the member until it is red, and place the sinuses on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full, and fall out, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, then apply it, for this helps greatly.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the place with ash, and then with water, very well, and then apply it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too quickly over the blood vessels, moisten the linen cloth with cold water, and apply it until the bleeding is stopped;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bleeding is profuse, then apply ground vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place on the area half-cooked peeled beans, and leave them until they burn at the site, it will stop the bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and if the veins do not want to take [the blood], then rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle there until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they sense the blood, they attach themselves;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they fall, then sprinkle a bit of ground aloes and seal, or ash, and they will now fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish physician disregards this chapter, who never saw any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the knowledge is rare in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject with knowledge, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, you must hurry to treat the patient from one side and the other, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or fainting, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If the body is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold things, that is to say cold broths, and meat of chicken and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, or of the spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	the patient returns to the first regimen he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with foods that produce great nourishment where there is viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the break repairs itself more quickly and better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of old and frail people cannot heal or knit well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but has no care, reset on the broken bone the thick tendon that binds and joins the limb together, until it is reinforced as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and does not spoil any part of its work, and for that reason it is necessary to nourish with coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go across, and others in sharpening, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each method have its own ingenuity and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory comes into place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the bone fracture is known by the twisted limb, and clearly appears due to deficiency, and sounds on pressing with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have a twist, or a split, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it by hand, but apply medicines that come after here, and then bind it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break going through, where the two parts are separated, they must now be placed evenly together, so that hot abscesses may come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come, then leave it for some days until the abscesses are calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it equal to the movement that you can do lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of that which has pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then bind it as appropriate thereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, then stretch it with two parts, if it is hands or feet, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset all the fragments in their places as much as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and align the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not properly aligned:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	so she raises it beautifully, and does not tighten too much, nor presses as those who cause by their work a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set right, then instruct the patient well that he does not move it, neither while waking nor sleeping, nor in turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, then it is not set right, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straight, so no deformity comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	one must wrap cloths of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	one must wrap with a wide and hard binding, for the wide bindings encircle the entire large limb and compress it equally on all sides, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind around light splints, three or four turns according to the limb, and compress your hand a bit along the entire binding, then go above the break and compress less, so that the break may extend slightly;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy area, then take another ligament, and wrap it around the broken area again;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break, and bind it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first section above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place linen or cloths between the ligaments until it is all even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something that alleviates the abscess when warm, and which reduces the swelling, and leave it like this for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then cut onto your splints, and let them be half the width of a large cane, shaped carefully, or made from wood used for plows, or palm ribs, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one places on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as is necessary for the member's smallness or largeness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind onto the splints just as you have done at the first place, then tie on top a suitable thread, as in the first place on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter afterwards, then less tight;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, like I have seen in the works of fools who make their stitches like cords from twisted linen, and this is great error, for the stitch cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than a finger's breadth between each needle.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the arrows after they are embedded in their flesh, put under them tow of linen, or shredded wool, so that it does not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the skin is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all broken limbs of arrows on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put in stitches that after five days or seven, or more according to your security from a hot abscess coming on;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the method of the ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take the flour that sticks to the mill walls, and knead it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method for the plaster restoring the break in various situations, especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method for the plaster restoring the break and the dislocation and the twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take б of bay leaves and labdanum and anil and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, total X б.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, total V б.
alechil VIIII З.;	apply nine aleches;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix it with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the person is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and mallows, an equal amount;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	mastic and aloe, nine dirhams each;
acaice VI З.;	acetum six dirhams;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	boil Armenian rhubarb X З., and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of plaster for joints and bones out of their places, and to alleviate the pain that follows, and the shards use of the bone, and the fracture:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and melt it in grease and in cooked oil, and apply it to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried fig leaves and earthbind leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of mallows, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making a stronger plaster than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of mallows, and flaxseed, buckthorn, sweet clover, and sorrel, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb to restore strength anything other than a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between two neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says one should put on the broken limb to restore dry things a bit warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of poultice that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mutton fat and human nails that have been cut off, or bird feathers, and vervain, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	do not loosen it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the poultice now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and moist sea sponge, and soak it in water, and apply it to the place until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage until you are sure of a warm abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is removed, then start the gentle binding again, and apply a poultice, but do not squeeze as tightly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for it gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen has been entirely removed, and you need plaster and binding, then restart it as you have done before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	and if none of what we have said applies to the limb, do not untie it until after three or four or five or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is observed, until the fracture heals, and the flesh grows over the alignment;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then hold it tighter than before, and swell its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the area drying more than is necessary, know that no healing can come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then use warm water, every time you release it, and do this every third day, and slightly reduce the dressing;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work then comes the healing to the limb, and quickly amends what the foolish doctors do, who restore the limb improperly:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is harmful, and it is fearful work, and I see nothing else but letting it be and treating it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various manners of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures exist, and various shapes, and their causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone down to the surface that is beneath the bone, just as an ax splits wood;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for that reason this kind of fracture is called "hatchet blow".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, this kind of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wounds of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a split from the edge of a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the tissue that is under the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And there is a wound that penetrates the bone as finely as a hair, and the split is small, and for that reason this fracture is called "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made by striking a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and makes the piece of the bone go inwards, and the place is twisted like how the blacksmiths strike on the cauldrons;
si entre li piere dedens.	and the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are separated like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all sorts of fractures by cutting into them, and by probing attempts, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is understood by this, that when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, beware of the patient's accidents, and if you see any harmful signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stiffness, paleness, ague fever, eyes coming out forcefully and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no astonishing accident and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue under the bone be corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	and if the bone fracture extends to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and expose over the bone in all ways that you can, and over the face of the wound as much as you can, and if blood flows out when exposing the bone, or an abscess is hot, aid with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and be sure of the flow of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and they should be made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you must pierce around it, either by making cuts with probes, but not so deeply that they do not penetrate beyond the skull bone, and there should be a margin or circle above the tip to prevent the point from passing beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several, so that each comes into its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have probes for all skulls;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and these are the forms of the three types of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	and the quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one tarer on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the tarer in another part a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or with any of the tools you have such as tongs, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone perforated and drawn out, then it is necessary that you remove the roughness which remains on the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be finer and more delicate than other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any of the small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then cleanse the wound with tents and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of work is the one that Galen said, which is simpler;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone where the fracture shows movement, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which here is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the part to be cut is on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be careful of the tissue that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, remove it lightly, for it should be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the skin, and the bone is only cut on top, and there are small fragments, then it is necessary to address that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various sizes, to apply in each place most appropriately, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	And scrape first with large scrapers, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, you must treat according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another piece of linen folded in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first piece of linen;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can, so you do not burden the surface, then apply another bandage on top, and do not bind it too tightly, only enough for it to reach the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like this for one or two days until the hot abscess is calmed, then untie it, and apply medications such as lily roots, and bran of beans, and incense powder, and aristotle, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer immediately cleansing medicines without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is immediately clean, do not leave any ointment, nor allow scabs to form, for when scabs form on the fabric of the brain, they can corrupt and harm it, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put something biting on the surface, it can burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	and if blackening comes on it other than from the medicine you have put on, which has such virtue, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them, and put it on the surface;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with methods of treatments that are necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for there are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not cause to cave in or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should put your little finger into the nostril, and place that break inside according to your finger's guidance, and push by force, until the nose returns to its natural form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the fingers cannot reach the place, then you must make it even with the tip of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	and if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess is calmed, then place at the head of the nail pieces of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	And you place another on the other side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the pieces be so thick that they fill the holes of the nail.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some say that one should moisten the threads with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me, but they must be moistened with egg white and mill powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent, until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in place of tents, and thus wraps the cloth around, and the surgeon holds it, and the patient blows through;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, put a poultice or cotton moistened with rose oil, or with a drop of mercury.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if hot abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster for cooling, of flaxseed flour, and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light bandages on top, and do not bind the limb;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break of the limb is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for that, then sew the wound, and treat with things that heal flesh and promote healing, such as appropriate plasters and ointments;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it has no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in pins of pitch until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured below, and there is no open wound, and the break is only superficial, and is not split into two, but rather indented inward, it is recognized as a minor injury.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the break is on the left jaw, then put your index finger of the right hand, and push the break inside gently, and align it with the other hand by force, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from both parts until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs or a tear, then extract them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then put on the broken jaw a poultice, and place a double cloth over it;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the cloth a well-made large needle or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as high as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	and if you see that the face changes, untie it on the third day, and then reapply precisely what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put a poultice on, of the powder from the mill with egg white or sesame flour, after you have removed the plaster;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on the poultice a light wool, and if the poultices dry out and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, treat it if no piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so carefully remove the fragments with appropriate instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and apply appropriate poultices to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forearm breaks often in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated into two, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forearm is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the fracture equally in your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor shift.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch more, then place under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of cloth, or of wool, and let it be large according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the forearm, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you place the fracture equally as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back into place due to its being stuck, then it is necessary for the patient to lie often on his side, and put under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the attendant push the shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	and then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, then you must split it open;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull lightly on the fragments, and if the bone cannot join due to some obstacle, then cut it with one of the incisors that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place under the forceps this instrument, to protect the surface:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not closed, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and let it have two ends, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the rupture of the wound that you made when you pulled the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt it is a hot abscess, then apply cloths and bandages to the wound according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, moisten the cloth with rose oil and with asses' fat and with wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when there are no wounds and no cutting, is that you put on the bone a plaster of mill powder and egg white, and place light bandages over it, and put a sphere under the splint if you need it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage of a palm in width, then place the doubled cloth over the bandages and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin strip three digits wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the strip on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy splint, and under the diseased splint;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the reset of each part, and when you see that the bone holds the break properly, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the bindings loosen, restrain it again;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small bolster under the mattress when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	thus lighten the break of the arm by the elevation of the shoulder, where you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind it unless bad accidents occur, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the plaster if you see it is needed, and bind it tightly, leaving it this way until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in twenty-eight days or less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	and it often happens that the shoulder is broken at its broad part or in the middle, and one does not know it except by touching it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then apply flour from the mill with egg white and light bandages, and place a double cloth on top;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin board slightly larger than the shoulder, and if beneath the board there are any hollows in the shoulder, fill those hollows with flax bandages so that the board lies evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then it is tightly bound with a large bandage firmly, so that the splinter does not move from its place, and check the binding every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it becomes soft, it is bound, and the splinter is placed back in its proper place if it has moved, and the patient lies on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, then untie it, and be sure, for it is not bone that moves easily out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points below the heart, cut above it, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the arm to ease an abscess that is hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the hip
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the root.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain, lacks strength, becomes faint, and may vomit blood, and the marrow appears in the broken bone, which can be clearly seen.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and you place a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs from the second rib with your hands, and delicately apply equal pressure in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then apply plasters and bandages over the stake subtly of salt, or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and lay it on the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and bind it gently, and loosen the bandage every hour, and if it becomes soft, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be loosed, for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and loosen it, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come in ways of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the plaster again, and bind it until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of the ribs only occurs in their thick parts behind the back, and at the head inward, and they do not bend except because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one can feel it well upon examination with the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is to set the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of the ribs inclines inward, then the patient feels great pain and pricking, like from pleurisy, for the bone pricks the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and a punctured wound, and quickly it causes great spewing of blood, and this is from severe illness, and the elders have put much ingenuity into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And so there are some who say that one must administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the wind downwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not wish for hot abscesses to occur if they have not already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has occurred, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say that we put leeches on the place to suck well, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	however, there is doubt that the leeches may not draw the excess to the place due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the warmth around, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision over the site of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to support the surface;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if hot abscesses come, then put on cloths moistened in rose oil, and place them on the area;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as appropriate for an abscess, and let the patient lie on their side where it is needed until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes the neck bones are fractured, and it may happen that it bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and likewise for the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then beware if you see his hands softened, swollen, and lifeless, and he cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the bone’s joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it will be healed or not, then beware if the feet are softened, and if the symptoms are present which are in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary emission;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it is treated on its belly, there is involuntary emission.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to saddle up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	do not labor too much in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you wrap it if there is a hot abscess, put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on it and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on the part where the pain is felt until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cut on the joint;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, then treat it with ointment to promote healing until he is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the skull," place your pouched hand (left), and make it equal to the other hand as much as possible, then put the plaster and the splint on top if needed;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then he tightens it, and if there is dislocated bone, he cuts over it, removes it, and treats the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction at the top;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it lengthens outward and tilts inward, and the patient feels pain in the area, and there is a sharpness and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you place your hand over it until you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and understand where the break is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is at the head alone, then set equal this fracture, until it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it tilts inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is aligned for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	and when you have set it equal, then put on the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the area beneath the ribs until the swelling is equalized.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
