Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	and if hot abscesses come, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are calmed, and put on what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and bind it as appropriate, if there is no harmful accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a stick of moderate thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends with two bindings, and pull them up, and seat the patient on a chair;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then lay his broken arm on the stick until it reaches the shoulder, and place a wooden support in the middle, then pull upwards with some weight or have an assistant stretch it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then the physician places the splint equally with both hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that the patient is placed on his back, and his hand is tied to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below all the way to the joint, and each stretches their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish that the extraction be stronger, then hold the limb below the fracture and above the fracture, and stretch each of the assistants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the splint is close to the shoulder, then you must place one tie in the middle under the axilla, and the other towards the side, under the splint;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and likewise if the splint is towards the side, then you must place the bandage lightly, without force, until the splint is even on the spot and on the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then set the fracture evenly as it should be, and bind it, if no warm abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if warm abscesses come, then do not bind it for seven days, and place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on it until the warm abscesses are calmed;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then you bind it, and the method of binding is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then align the arm with the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and place the bandage, and bind it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you fear that the bone may move, then use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three inches beyond the fracture on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then extract on the stars, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, more strongly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stars and the binding, as we have said, at the hour when you restore the broken limb, and you fear the abscess is hot, then leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine the bandage every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not arise in the area, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is directed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen it until after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place beneath the shoulder a cushion full of wool evenly, and look at each hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the ligaments do not become softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	and direct it through the power of medicine, and give it the meat that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the meat be at first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, let it be coarser.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be fully recovered in forty days;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one should untie it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to properly direct the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and embedded, it remains to untie for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "radius", of which one is small, and it is the one that follows the wrist;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps only the large radius is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small radius is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fragment that is merely broken, then it should be gently extended and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large radius, then it must be bound more tightly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it on the cushion, and raise the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, that the patient does not suffer any strain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the minister's arm below to his hand, or to the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the doctor should place it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, then place each in its place, and if any detached piece pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut into it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the splint for the wound, I have spoken of it in a specific chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the healing process abscesses occur, then apply a cloth with ointment made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the cloth on top gently, until the heated abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	and then remove the plaster, and put on the poultice of mill powder with egg white, then place the splints, and let the splint of the brace be stronger right away and a bit wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six splints on the arm in various arrangements:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and bind tighter on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less tightly as you move away, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is sewn, be of flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must rinse the member with warm water, until the itchings are calmed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member rest without being too tight.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the binding again, and if the joint is loosened and the bones separated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be wary if the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a bit, and leave it this way for some days until the nourishment circulates, and then bind it tightly.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or wrap around, then he can place his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and jolting, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the joints of the fingers there are few breaks, and they do not come more often than a sprain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	and when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sits crossed, and sits straight in front of him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the stretched cloth, and the minister stretches the broken bones, and the doctors make them equal until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and the bandages, if no abscesses come, then put a splint according to the size of the area;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is on the outside around the belly of the foot, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it tightly as appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is in the palm, then you must put a splint on top and another beneath in the sole, so that the hand be open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the break comes to any of the joints of the fingers, if it is swollen, then make it even as appropriate;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bind it with the sole, and if you wish, put a small straight splint to elevate the break, and do not move it;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is in the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, then make it even, and bind it with the healthy finger that comes after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	When you tie them all while holding, which is better, or you put on a splint, just like in a poultice;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the placement of a hot abscess, and support those who come to it, just as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is such that you bind one end above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends his bandage equally on his side;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the hip, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	and likewise if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be close to the knee, and let the extension be downwards;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then the physician places the bone straight with his two hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then applies the plaster, and binds it, if no abscesses come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	and if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the binding is done in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture one thick bandage doubled into two or three layers and leave the excess, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the knee, and place one long thread between the thigh and the leg, below close to the knee, and let the ends of the thread come above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn over the bandage on the leg and on the thigh, then place the splints in position, and put a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then place the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to evenly distribute the pressure, then begin to tightly bind three or four turns on the splint;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher up the splint, apply less pressure;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then tighten the two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and the thigh, and bind three splints that are above, then go back down to the top of the thread until you come near the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and he restrains it so that it does not move from its place, then leaves it thus, until no abscess or swelling or similar comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens there, he loosens it and addresses what comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that cause pain, then it must be washed, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut open the place and draw out pus;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	and sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that one must insert splints, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, in the restoration thus made, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 50 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the region of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not more than a crack, or perforation, and it happens to all wounds, both visible and invisible, and this people feel well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one puts equal pressure on what is round to its ends, until it is assembled so that it can move;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and place a round splint if you need it, and bind it as appropriate, then treat all the conditions we have mentioned in other fractures, such as a hot abscess and similar ones;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	apply to each case what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is properly called "tibia," and the other is called "fibula";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it happens that all kinds of fractures are like those in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is as with that of the arm equally, and the work is entirely so. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen;
et torne desoz.	and it turns inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	then apply extension, and make it even, and bind the splints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, if the fracture is bad and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and lighten according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that fit the leg on one side and the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap one bandage over and under them in two places, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not be able to deviate to the right or left, and thus it is properly secured;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some administer one board as long as the leg, and if it is made of wood, the leg is placed there to prevent movement, and this is properly done in a fracture where there is an injury;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle no fracture occurs, but sometimes a fracture happens to the bones of the foot and less so to the toes, and there is force that shatters in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see these bones protrude over each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground as if they wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of theirs where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the plaster and bandages on top, and place under the arch of the foot a small board two fingers thick, then bind it to the foot appropriately, after you have wrapped cloths around, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then loosen the binding, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the fingers are broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place a splint on the broken finger according to the length of the finger, and let it be a bit wider, then put beneath the end that tablet I have mentioned, and bind it appropriately;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint on each finger according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the tablet beneath the end;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed at the head of the tablet to support the belly of the end, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to other breakers, since we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and address each incident as it is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, have her sit stretched out, then incline her towards the back part, and let her be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the patient's female part with cotton, and put as much in there as a thumb;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand the woman up, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton comes out, until it reaches the entrance of her female part, and the bone returns with it;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, she removes the cotton, and after she has urinated, she puts it back, and thus does this for seven days or around:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	the fracture will be restored, and if you want, take a bladder of a bird, tie a reed to the opening, and insert the whole bladder into the appropriate place;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the reed forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the fracture will then return to its natural state;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and leave it this way for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or a woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and they are not hidden these fractures coming to those who put their study and practice into it, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fractures indicate in various positions the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or a bit longer, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cauterized now, so that the cauterizations we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then stop it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the broken area at that same hour, or on that day, unless hot abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses come, then delay the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscesses are calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered chest, then you must set it lightly with your hands, with slight stretching.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not available to make it equal in your hands, then reset it with this instrument which is made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the doctor to apply three or four, according to what he needs in each case of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and a bit thick, so that it does not bend when pressed on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle to the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palette," therefore the bent head of the bone should be placed on top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it once, until it returns, and make them equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is fine and the instruments cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the head of the bone so that the instruments may have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	and if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, or an incisor or saw, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then scrape what remains in the bone of roughness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is replaced and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	so do this until it is in its place, then moisten the bandage with black styptic wine, and clean if it is necessary;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound any salve or other oily substance that might cause putrefaction and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then apply bandages when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times this has been done by foolish doctors, and they have caused the patient death or corruption at times;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the bindings be softer and looser than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that harmful accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then you should not put stones on it;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, instead of stones, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two the wound around the wound inflame, remove what you have put on with all wine, and apply a healing salve, such as tetrafarmacon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and whole.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the pus flows down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but keeps coming back with pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other kind of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not treat it, for often death results, but leave it until it putrefies;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perchance it will fall off by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come upon the joint
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often see the health of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a gruesome thing to look at the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Be careful then if the wound is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	administer styptic medicines to it, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, gallnuts, and similar others, so that you take any one of these things, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and he places them on the knot in bundles, and binds them well, and does not untie them for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocates it, and begins another one, until the knots are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	where you extract on a well-made piece of flesh;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the flesh is such that it removes all swellings above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has already hardened like stone and needs to be removed, then cut on top of it and open the visible excess;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	where you shave it with a razor until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone fracture is restored, and the limbs remain weak and delicate afterwards, it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bindings, and the nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or due to an abundance of bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or due to excessive movements, not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, thus is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and soften the body so that the blood may multiply within him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and the minister bathes, and gives joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then puts pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts to the large swelling, and often waters it with warm water, until the swelling runs to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed limb after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is visible, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb all over again, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and great evils come from it, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the nodules and the swellings are fresh, then they should be soaked in hot water, or herbs that soften should be boiled, such as leaves of mallows, and roots, and mallows, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and he makes the softening plaster, such as diaquilon well does, and you take the mallow mucilage, and mix it with hen's fat or linseed oil, and make a plaster on top;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fatty figs, and grind them with coloquintida, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodulation is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the limb be moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the twisted part is awakened and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it must be cut until the bone, with a subtle light incision;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply care and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then he must now bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the joint swells, and perhaps it is reset with difficulty in its place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore, one should not move it at the time when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	it often causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient sweat, then leave it alone until the abscesses have calmed;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each limb as the treatment will bring it back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It often happens that the jaws are dislocated here, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are slightly displaced from their places, and somewhat softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are entirely dislocated, and hang downwards, causing the saliva to flow from the mouth so that he cannot hold it in, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is wrapped around his speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through many arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and whole, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and the doctor places a small bag from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other fingers of the hands should be apart, to make equal;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instructs the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician places it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the resetting is difficult, especially if both jaws are dislocated together, then wash them with warm water and oil until you reset them gently;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay in resetting them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well without softening, then put on cloths moistened in an unguent made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft bindings;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor exert himself to mix, but take light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then chew what he wants lightly, and do not strain to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and mended.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be perfectly reset within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fevers and usual sweats result, and perhaps diarrhea occurs, and perhaps vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times the one to whom it happens dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from the side within the continuity of the breast and the swelling, and it sometimes dislocates outward, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies alone on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and bind it, and constrict it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint that is towards the side cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and bandage it, and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way is reset the shoulder of the spine when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except according to three manners:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it dislocates on the side of the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is on the side of the breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and occasionally it dislocates on the upper side, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder, and does not dislocate inward due to the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocates downward towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it happens quickly and suddenly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	in those who have enough flesh, it happens with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens to some men that there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you test it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And the dislocation is known when it moves downward towards the socket, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a noticeable difference between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and beneath the collarbone by touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move it in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the patient is young.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his thumbs beneath the collarbone, and raises the joint forcefully upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then places it below;
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	and if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the administrator uses a strongly soothing and relaxing agent, such as a decoction of hellebore and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then place the patient on their back, and put under the board a piece of wool equally neither too soft nor too hard, then the doctor places his heel on the piece, and lifts the head of the shoulder forcefully, and pulls the patient's arm;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister holds the head of the patient so it does not move down;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder returns completely now, and if you want to reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you have a man present who is taller than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand straight against the side, and place his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit up so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another minister pulls the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him some heavy thing may help, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also reset in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and one sticks the long firebrand into the ground, so that the shoulder is as hard as a pestle, and neither too large nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but that there be cloths above, and the patient be lying along the long part of the wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand should be stretched down on the other side properly, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return despite all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take the firebrand two arms in length and four fingers in width, which has the head hard to insert under the skin, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie above the head of the wooden stake with underclothes, so that the wood does not wound the patient, then place it under the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm over the long stake, and tie the shoulder to the stake, and the arm at the hand, then place the arm on a step of a broad ladder, and let the hand hang down, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint is now in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner, you must put under the armpit a sphere of equal wool, then apply a poultice mixed with mill powder, along with incense and egg white, on all over the shoulder and around, then strain under the armpit appropriately, and wrap the bandage over the poultice, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and it is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is displaced due to moisture that has come in, or for other reasons, then you must apply cauterization at three points, as it is set out in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	and if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm up, then you know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or weakened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the breast or behind is done by pushing and stretching with the hands, and another place is administered;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing there comes cracking in the limb, and slowness in movement, then the patient should take baths many times, until that cracking is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated little by little, and little by little returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has dislocated entirely, especially in front and back, and the dislocation is not put back, for it is clearly seen and felt;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it before hot abscesses occur, for if hot abscesses were to come, it would be difficult to reset;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be returned, you extend his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms be spread out, and the hands of the physician according to the cut around, above and below, and put the joint at its angles together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he folds his hand to his hand, and trust in the root of the palm the part that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two assistants extend the arm, and two assistants hold it so that it does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the doctor joins the joint with his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then forcefully pushes the joint back until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, he puts on a dry plaster with egg white, then tightly binds it, ties the arm to the patient's neck, and leaves it for some days, then unbinds it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	and if the joint is firm in its place, then untie the binding, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the plaster and the binding, and leave it this way for some days until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is reset, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is eased;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or place a piece of fat sheep’s grease on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the grease back on, and then enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you wish, put warm cow dung mixed with butter on it and apply it;
si revenra a sa disposition.	so it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is light, more than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, lest the area swell or a hot abscess form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is such that you place the afflicted hand on a table, and the assistant stretches the hand, and the doctor places his hand equally, so that he puts his palm on the surface of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, you must check if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then place the patient’s back of his hand on a table at the extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then place the patient's back of his hand upon the table, and the physician places his hand upon that area of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	if it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	if not, then apply warm poultices to soothe the abscesses, and leave it thus without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	and if he cannot bear it, and you cannot place it back in position after some days, then the joint will remain distorted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it does not harm the patient's strength as long as the hand is weakened, and cannot grasp anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	so there is no other way stronger than to draw close with cautery near the case, and by chance there may be nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any crack, then soften it with hot water, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the front;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then extend the finger and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then hold the tip of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is separated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, then make it straight on the third day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and at night bind it as we have said, and unbind it during the day, and make it move, and bind it again at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the vertebrae of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebrae of the back or neck are dislocated, or there are several dislocated, there is no cure, for death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the excretions jump out without will, and cannot be held back, and many times some member is weakened, or both thighs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the shadow changes in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which changes at the back is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is that you reward if the lameness has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	there shall be no treatment nor healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And for those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment speak greatly in grand words, which do not have much real benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the lameness which comes to the front foot, there is no remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and likewise that which comes directly to both sides, and one cannot cure except properly the one that comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have straw underneath him, so he does not hurt himself;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick the poker firmly in the ground at the head and the other at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the arms of the patient, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two pokers;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be well secured, the pokers as we have said, and the doctors place their palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient lie on their side, and put the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you wish, do it with a wrench that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should drive in two stakes at the head of the patient's length of a large arm, and towards the feet two others, and have between each stake, above and below, a palm's space in length;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each firebrand one hole, where the drill turns, and let the firebrands be firmly in the ground so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two firebrands have one rotating firebrand, on which the ropes turn, and in two rotations have two small firebrands of one palm long, to turn the drill;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the rope that is among the boards to the drill towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other drill, and each of the assistants turns his drill along the entire rope, and the master places the point equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equal, place a drying plaster with plenty of egg, and then the wadding, and then the splint of a piece three inches long, which should cover the area of swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a rope as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until he is healed;
